<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">Casualties and losses</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="width:50%;border-right:1px dotted #aaa;">
<p><b>Britain:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>60,000 civilians killed<sup id="cite_ref-White_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li>160,000 airmen (Europe)<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><b>China:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>260,000–351,000 Chinese civilians<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><b>France:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>67,000 civilians killed<sup id="cite_ref-France_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France-7">[7]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><b>The Netherlands:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Thousands of civilians</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Poland:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Tens of thousands of civilians</li>
</ul>
<p><b>USSR:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>More than 500,000 Soviet civilians<sup id="cite_ref-Hawley_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hawley-8">[8]</a></sup></li>
<li>2,700 airmen (Japan)<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:50%;padding-left:0.25em">
<p><b>Germany:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>353,000–635,000 civilians killed, including foreign workers<sup id="cite_ref-White_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Germany_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Germany-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
<li>Very heavy damage to industry</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Japan:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>330,000–500,000 civilians killed<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
<li>Very heavy damage to industry</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Italy:</b></p>
<ul>
<li>60,000–100,000 civilians killed<sup id="cite_ref-Marco_Gioannini_p._491_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marco_Gioannini_p._491-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li>5,000 soldiers killed<sup id="cite_ref-Marco_Gioannini_p._491_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marco_Gioannini_p._491-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li>Heavy damage to industry</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>

<p><b>Contemporaneous wars</b></p>
<dl>
<dd><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Civil_War" title="Chinese Civil War">Chinese Civil War</a></dd>

</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p><b>Strategic bombing during World War II</b> was the sustained <a href="/wiki/Aerial_warfare" title="Aerial warfare">aerial attack</a> on railways, harbours, cities, workers' housing, and industrial districts in enemy territory during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing" title="Strategic bombing">Strategic bombing</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Military_strategy" title="Military strategy">military strategy</a> which is distinct from both <a href="/wiki/Close_air_support" title="Close air support">close air support</a> of ground forces and <a href="/wiki/Air_supremacy#World_War_II" title="Air supremacy">tactical air power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>During World War II, it was believed by many military strategists of <a href="/wiki/Air_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Air power">air power</a> that major victories could be won by attacking industrial and political infrastructure, rather than purely military targets.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Strategic bombing often involved bombing areas inhabited by civilians and some campaigns were deliberately designed to target civilian populations in order to terrorize and disrupt their usual activities. <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">International law</a> at the outset of World War II did not specifically forbid aerial bombardment of cities despite the prior occurrence of such bombing during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">Second Sino-Japanese War</a>.</p>
<p>Strategic bombing during World War II began on 1 September 1939 when Germany invaded Poland and the <i><a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a></i> (German Air Force) <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Wielu%C5%84" title="Bombing of Wieluń">began bombing cities</a> and the civilian population in Poland in an indiscriminate <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Warsaw_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Warsaw in World War II">aerial bombardment campaign</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> As the war continued to expand, bombing by both the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> increased significantly. The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> began bombing Germany in March 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In September 1940, the Luftwaffe began targeting British cities in '<a href="/wiki/The_Blitz" title="The Blitz">The Blitz</a>'.<sup id="cite_ref-Murray_1983.2C_p._52_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray_1983.2C_p._52-17">[17]</a></sup> After the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</a> in June 1941, the Luftwaffe attacked Soviet cities and infrastructure. From 1942 onward, the British bombing campaign against Germany became <a href="/wiki/Area_bombing_directive" title="Area bombing directive">less restrictive</a> and increasingly targeted industrial sites and eventually, civilian areas.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Garrett_1993_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garrett_1993-19">[19]</a></sup> When the United States began flying bombing missions against Germany, it reinforced these efforts and controversial firebombings were carried out against <a href="/wiki/Operation_Gomorrah" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Gomorrah">Hamburg</a> (1943), <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Dresden_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Dresden in World War II">Dresden</a> (1945), and other German cities.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a>, the Japanese bombed civilian populations throughout the war (e.g. in <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Chongqing" title="Bombing of Chongqing">Chongqing</a>). The US <a href="/wiki/Air_raids_on_Japan" title="Air raids on Japan">air raids on Japan</a> began in earnest in October 1944<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and by March 1945 had started their escalation into widespread <a href="/wiki/Firebombing" title="Firebombing">firebombing</a>, which culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki</a> on 6 and 9 August 1945, respectively.</p>
<p>The effect of strategic bombing was highly debated during and after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-anesi.com_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anesi.com-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-J.K._Galbraith_1958_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J.K._Galbraith_1958-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Williamson_Murray_p._319_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williamson_Murray_p._319-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-econ.yale.edu_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-econ.yale.edu-25">[25]</a></sup> Both the <i>Luftwaffe</i> and RAF failed to deliver a knockout blow by destroying enemy morale. However some argued that strategic bombing of non-military targets could significantly reduce enemy industrial capacity and production<sup id="cite_ref-Buckley_1998.2C_p._165_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buckley_1998.2C_p._165-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Murray_1983.2C_p._253_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Murray_1983.2C_p._253-27">[27]</a></sup> and in the opinion of its <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a> proponents, the surrender of Japan vindicated strategic bombing.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>
