<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties">Casualties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Casualties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fotothek_df_ps_0000047_Eine_Mutter_%C3%BCber_dem_Kinderwagen_ihrer_Zwillinge_im_Tode.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fotothek_df_ps_0000047_Eine_Mutter_%C3%BCber_dem_Kinderwagen_ihrer_Zwillinge_im_Tode.jpg/220px-Fotothek_df_ps_0000047_Eine_Mutter_%C3%BCber_dem_Kinderwagen_ihrer_Zwillinge_im_Tode.jpg" width="220" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fotothek_df_ps_0000047_Eine_Mutter_%C3%BCber_dem_Kinderwagen_ihrer_Zwillinge_im_Tode.jpg/330px-Fotothek_df_ps_0000047_Eine_Mutter_%C3%BCber_dem_Kinderwagen_ihrer_Zwillinge_im_Tode.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Fotothek_df_ps_0000047_Eine_Mutter_%C3%BCber_dem_Kinderwagen_ihrer_Zwillinge_im_Tode.jpg/440px-Fotothek_df_ps_0000047_Eine_Mutter_%C3%BCber_dem_Kinderwagen_ihrer_Zwillinge_im_Tode.jpg 2x" data-file-width="783" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fotothek_df_ps_0000047_Eine_Mutter_%C3%BCber_dem_Kinderwagen_ihrer_Zwillinge_im_Tode.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Civilian casualties in <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a> after allied bombing on the night of February 13, 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the war, the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Bombing_Survey" class="mw-redirect" title="Strategic Bombing Survey">Strategic Bombing Survey</a> reviewed the available <a href="/wiki/Casualty_(person)" title="Casualty (person)">casualty</a> records in Germany, and concluded that official German statistics of casualties from air attack had been too low. The survey estimated that at a minimum 305,000 were killed in German cities due to bombing and estimated a minimum of 780,000 wounded. Roughly 7,500,000 German civilians were also rendered homeless. (see <a href="/wiki/Dehousing" title="Dehousing">Dehousing</a>). Overy estimated in 2014 that in all about 353,000 civilians were killed by British and American bombing of German cities.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to the minimum figure given in the Strategic bombing survey, the number of people killed by Allied bombing in Germany has been estimated at between 400,000 and 600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Germany_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Germany-10">[10]</a></sup> In the UK, 60,595 British were killed by German bombing,<sup id="cite_ref-White_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White-2">[2]</a></sup> and in France, 67,078 French were killed by US-UK bombing.<sup id="cite_ref-France_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Belgrade was heavily bombed by the Luftwaffe on 6 April 1941, when more than 17,000 people were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> According to <i>The Oxford companion to World War II</i>, "After Italy's surrender the Allies kept up the bombing of the northern part occupied by the Germans and more than 50,000 Italians were killed in these raids."<sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford-198">[198]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Statistics_(Italy)" title="National Institute of Statistics (Italy)">Istat</a> study of 1957 stated that 64,354 Italians were killed by aerial bombing, 59,796 of whom were civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-Marco_Gioannini_p._491_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marco_Gioannini_p._491-12">[12]</a></sup> Historians Marco Gioannini and Giulio Massobrio argued in 2007 that this figure is inaccurate due to loss of documents, confusion and gaps, and estimated the total number of civilian casualties in Italy due to aerial bombing as comprised between 80,000 and 100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over 160,000 Allied airmen and 33,700 planes were lost in the <a href="/wiki/European_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European theatre of World War II">European theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (May 2010)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Casualties_of_a_mass_panic_-_Chungking,_China.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Casualties_of_a_mass_panic_-_Chungking%2C_China.jpg/170px-Casualties_of_a_mass_panic_-_Chungking%2C_China.jpg" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Casualties_of_a_mass_panic_-_Chungking%2C_China.jpg/255px-Casualties_of_a_mass_panic_-_Chungking%2C_China.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Casualties_of_a_mass_panic_-_Chungking%2C_China.jpg/340px-Casualties_of_a_mass_panic_-_Chungking%2C_China.jpg 2x" data-file-width="428" data-file-height="592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Casualties_of_a_mass_panic_-_Chungking,_China.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chinese casualties of a mass panic during a June 1941 Japanese aerial <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Chongqing" title="Bombing of Chongqing">bombing of Chongqing</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Within Asia, the majority of strategic bombing was carried out by the Japanese and the US. The British Commonwealth planned that once the war in Europe was complete, a strategic bombing force of up to 1,000 heavy bombers (<a href="/wiki/Tiger_Force_(air)" title="Tiger Force (air)">"Tiger Force"</a>) would be sent to the Far East. This was never realised before the end of the Pacific War.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Japanese_bombing">Japanese bombing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Japanese bombing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ChongqingBombing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a7/ChongqingBombing.jpg/220px-ChongqingBombing.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/a7/ChongqingBombing.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="165" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ChongqingBombing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a> during a bombing</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Japanese strategic bombing was independently conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Navy_Air_Service" title="Imperial Japanese Navy Air Service">Imperial Japanese Navy Air Service</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army_Air_Service" title="Imperial Japanese Army Air Service">Imperial Japanese Army Air Service</a>. Bombing efforts mostly targeted large Chinese cities such as <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Chongqing" title="Bombing of Chongqing">Chongqing</a>, with around 5,000 raids from February 1938 to August 1943 in the later case.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BattleOfShanghaiBaby_retouched.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleOfShanghaiBaby_retouched.jpg/220px-BattleOfShanghaiBaby_retouched.jpg" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleOfShanghaiBaby_retouched.jpg/330px-BattleOfShanghaiBaby_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BattleOfShanghaiBaby_retouched.jpg/440px-BattleOfShanghaiBaby_retouched.jpg 2x" data-file-width="587" data-file-height="477" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BattleOfShanghaiBaby_retouched.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A famous photo entitled <a href="/wiki/Bloody_Saturday_(photograph)" title="Bloody Saturday (photograph)">"Bloody Saturday"</a>, showing a burned and terrified baby in Shanghai's South Station following an IJN bombing</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The bombing of <a href="/wiki/Nanjing" title="Nanjing">Nanjing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a>, which began on 22 and 23 September 1937, called forth widespread protests culminating in a resolution by the Far Eastern Advisory Committee of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gascoyne-Cecil,_5th_Marquess_of_Salisbury" title="Robert Gascoyne-Cecil, 5th Marquess of Salisbury">Lord Cranborne</a>, the British Under-Secretary of State For Foreign Affairs, expressed his indignation in his own declaration.</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Words cannot express the feelings of profound horror with which the news of these raids had been received by the whole civilized world. They are often directed against places far from the actual area of hostilities. The military objective, where it exists, seems to take a completely second place. The main object seems to be to inspire terror by the indiscriminate slaughter of civilians...</p>
<div class="templatequotecite"><cite>— Lord Cranborne<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>There were also air raids on <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> and northern Australia (<a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Darwin_(February_1942)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombing of Darwin (February 1942)">Bombing of Darwin</a>, 19 February 1942). The Imperial Japanese Navy Air Service and the Imperial Japanese Army Air Service used tactical bombing against ships, airfields, military positions, and military installations, as the IJNAS had done at the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allied_bombing_of_South-East_Asia">Allied bombing of South-East Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Allied bombing of South-East Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_South-East_Asia_(1944%E2%80%9345)" title="Bombing of South-East Asia (1944–45)">Bombing of South-East Asia (1944–45)</a></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Thailand" title="Japanese invasion of Thailand">Japanese invasion of Thailand</a> (8 December 1941), the southeast Asian kingdom signed a treaty of alliance with Japan and declared war on the United States and the United Kingdom. The Allies dropped 18,583 bombs on Thailand during the war, resulting in the death of 8,711 people and the destruction of 9,616 buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> The primary target of the campaign was <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Bangkok_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Bangkok in World War II">Bangkok</a>, the Thai capital. Rural areas were almost entirely unaffected.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 1942, the United States <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Air_Force" title="Fourteenth Air Force">Fourteenth Air Force</a> based in southern China undertook the first air raids in <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a>. The American bombing campaign gained intensity after the surrender of Germany in May 1945, and by July Japanese defences were incapable of impeding their movement. The Americans had attained complete <a href="/wiki/Air_supremacy" title="Air supremacy">air supremacy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Victory_over_Japan" class="mw-redirect" title="Victory over Japan">victory over Japan</a>, on 19 August the denizens of <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a> broke into the streets and removed the black coverings off the street lamps.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1944–45, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Fleet" title="Eastern Fleet">Eastern Fleet</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> undertook several raids on the occupied <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_East_Indies" class="mw-redirect" title="Netherlands East Indies">Netherlands East Indies</a>. They also bombed the Japanese-occupied Indian territory of the <a href="/wiki/Andaman_and_Nicobar_Islands" title="Andaman and Nicobar Islands">Andaman and Nicobar Islands</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_bombing_of_Japan">United States bombing of Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: United States bombing of Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</div>
</td>
</tr>

<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Air_raids_on_Japan" title="Air raids on Japan">Air raids on Japan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japan_campaign" title="Japan campaign">Japan campaign</a></div>
<p>The United States began effective strategic bombing of Japan when <a href="/wiki/B-29_Superfortress" class="mw-redirect" title="B-29 Superfortress">B-29s</a> began operating from the Marianas (Guam and Tienen) in late 1944. Prior to that a single raid was launched from carriers in 1942, and ineffective long-range raids were launched from China from June to December 1944. In the last seven months of the campaign, a change to firebombing resulted in great destruction of 67 Japanese cities, as many as 500,000 Japanese deaths and some 5 million more made homeless. <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Hirohito" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor Hirohito">Emperor Hirohito</a>'s viewing of the destroyed areas of Tokyo in March 1945 is said to have been the beginning of his personal involvement in the peace process, culminating in <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">Japan's surrender</a> five months later.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conventional_bombing">Conventional bombing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Conventional bombing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(August 2009)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Firebombing_of_Tokyo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Firebombing_of_Tokyo.jpg/220px-Firebombing_of_Tokyo.jpg" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Firebombing_of_Tokyo.jpg/330px-Firebombing_of_Tokyo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Firebombing_of_Tokyo.jpg/440px-Firebombing_of_Tokyo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3152" data-file-height="2932" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Firebombing_of_Tokyo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tokyo burns during a <a href="/wiki/Firebombing" title="Firebombing">firebomb</a> attack 26 May 1945.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first U.S. raid on the Japanese main island was the <a href="/wiki/Doolittle_Raid" title="Doolittle Raid">Doolittle Raid</a> of 18 April 1942, when sixteen <a href="/wiki/B-25_Mitchell" class="mw-redirect" title="B-25 Mitchell">B-25 Mitchells</a> were launched from the <a href="/wiki/USS_Hornet_(CV-8)" title="USS Hornet (CV-8)">USS&#160;<i>Hornet</i>&#160;(CV-8)</a> to attack targets including <a href="/wiki/Yokohama" title="Yokohama">Yokohama</a> and Tokyo and then fly on to airfields in China. The raid was a military pinprick but a significant <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a> victory. Because they were launched prematurely, none of the aircraft had enough fuel to reach their designated landing sites, and so either crashed or ditched (except for one aircraft, which landed in the Soviet Union, where the crew was interned). Two crews were captured by the Japanese.</p>
<p>The key development for the bombing of Japan was the <a href="/wiki/B-29_Superfortress" class="mw-redirect" title="B-29 Superfortress">B-29 Superfortress</a>, which had an operational range of 1,500 miles (2,400&#160;km); almost 90% of the bombs (147,000 tons) dropped on the home islands of Japan were delivered by this bomber. The <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Yawata_(June_1944)" title="Bombing of Yawata (June 1944)">first raid by B-29s on Japan</a> was on 15 June 1944, from China. The B-29s took off from <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a>, over 1,500 miles away. This raid was also not particularly effective: only forty-seven of the sixty-eight bombers hit the target area.</p>
<p>Raids of Japan from mainland China, called <a href="/wiki/Operation_Matterhorn" title="Operation Matterhorn">Operation Matterhorn</a>, were carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Twentieth_Air_Force" title="Twentieth Air Force">Twentieth Air Force</a> under <a href="/wiki/XX_Bomber_Command" title="XX Bomber Command">XX Bomber Command</a>. Initially the commanding officer of the Twentieth Air Force was <a href="/wiki/Hap_Arnold" class="mw-redirect" title="Hap Arnold">Hap Arnold</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Curtis_LeMay" title="Curtis LeMay">Curtis LeMay</a>. Bombing Japan from China was never a satisfactory arrangement because not only were the Chinese airbases difficult to supply—materiel being sent by air from India over "<a href="/wiki/The_Hump" title="The Hump">the Hump</a>"—but the B-29s operating from them could only reach Japan if they traded some of their bomb load for extra fuel in tanks in the bomb-bays. When Admiral <a href="/wiki/Chester_Nimitz" class="mw-redirect" title="Chester Nimitz">Chester Nimitz</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Leapfrogging_(strategy)" title="Leapfrogging (strategy)">island-hopping</a> campaign captured Pacific islands close enough to Japan to be within the B-29's range, the Twentieth Air Force was assigned to <a href="/wiki/XXI_Bomber_Command" title="XXI Bomber Command">XXI Bomber Command</a>, which organized a much more effective bombing campaign of the Japanese home islands. Based in the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Marianas</a> (<a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tinian" title="Tinian">Tinian</a> in particular), the B-29s were able to carry their full bomb loads and were supplied by cargo ships and tankers. The first raid from the Mariana was on 24 November 1944, when 88 aircraft bombed Tokyo. The bombs were dropped from around 30,000 feet (10,000 m) and it is estimated that only around 10% hit their targets.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JapaneseCityDestroyedAreas.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/JapaneseCityDestroyedAreas.png/220px-JapaneseCityDestroyedAreas.png" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/JapaneseCityDestroyedAreas.png/330px-JapaneseCityDestroyedAreas.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/27/JapaneseCityDestroyedAreas.png/440px-JapaneseCityDestroyedAreas.png 2x" data-file-width="1743" data-file-height="1630" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JapaneseCityDestroyedAreas.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Conventional bombs from <a href="/wiki/Boeing_B-29_Superfortress" title="Boeing B-29 Superfortress">B-29s</a> destroyed over 40% of the urban area in Japan's six greatest industrial cities</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Unlike all other forces in theater, the <a href="/wiki/Bomber_Command#USAAF" title="Bomber Command">USAAF Bomber Commands</a> did not report to the commanders of the theaters but directly to the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a>. In July 1945, they were placed under the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Strategic_Air_Forces_in_the_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Strategic Air Forces in the Pacific">U.S. Strategic Air Forces in the Pacific</a>, which was commanded by General <a href="/wiki/Carl_Spaatz" class="mw-redirect" title="Carl Spaatz">Carl Spaatz</a>.</p>
<p>As in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">United States Army Air Forces</a> (USAAF) tried daylight <a href="/wiki/Precision_bombing" title="Precision bombing">precision bombing</a>. However, it proved to be impossible due to the weather around Japan, "during the best month for bombing in Japan, visual bombing was possible for [just] seven days. The worst had only one good day."<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> Further, bombs dropped from a great height were tossed about by high winds.</p>
<p>General LeMay, commander of XXI Bomber Command, instead switched to mass firebombing night attacks from altitudes of around 7,000 feet (2,100 m) on the major <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbations</a>. "He looked up the size of the large Japanese cities in the <i>World Almanac</i> and picked his targets accordingly."<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Priority targets were Tokyo, <a href="/wiki/Nagoya" title="Nagoya">Nagoya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kobe" title="Kobe">Kobe</a>. Despite limited early success, particularly against Nagoya, LeMay was determined to use such bombing tactics against the vulnerable Japanese cities. Attacks on strategic targets also continued in lower-level daylight raids.</p>
<p>The first successful <a href="/wiki/Firebombing" title="Firebombing">firebombing</a> raid was <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Kobe_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Kobe in World War II">on Kobe</a> on 3 February 1945, and following its relative success the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">USAAF</a> continued the tactic. Nearly half of the principal factories of the city were damaged, and production was reduced by more than half at one of the port's two shipyards.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Tokyo_in_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombing of Tokyo in World War II">The first raid of this type on Tokyo</a> was on the night of 23–24 February when 174 B-29s destroyed around one square mile (3&#160;km²) of the city. Following on that success, as <a href="/wiki/Operation_Meetinghouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Meetinghouse">Operation Meetinghouse</a>, 334 B-29s raided on the night of 9–10 March, of which 282 Superforts reached their targets, dropping around 1,700 tons of bombs. Around 16 square miles (41&#160;km²) of the city was destroyed and over 100,000 people are estimated to have died in the <a href="/wiki/Fire_storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Fire storm">fire storm</a>. It was the most destructive conventional raid, and the deadliest single bombing raid of any kind in terms of lives lost, in all of military aviation history,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> even when the missions on Hiroshima and Nagasaki are taken as single events.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> The city was made primarily of wood and paper, and the fires burned out of control. The effects of the Tokyo firebombing proved the fears expressed by Admiral <a href="/wiki/Isoroku_Yamamoto" title="Isoroku Yamamoto">Yamamoto</a> in 1939: "Japanese cities, being made of wood and paper, would burn very easily. The Army talks big, but if war came and there were large-scale air raids, there's no telling what would happen."<sup id="cite_ref-Spector_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spector-212">[212]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_kushu_1945-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Tokyo_kushu_1945-2.jpg/220px-Tokyo_kushu_1945-2.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Tokyo_kushu_1945-2.jpg/330px-Tokyo_kushu_1945-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Tokyo_kushu_1945-2.jpg/440px-Tokyo_kushu_1945-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="700" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_kushu_1945-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The charred remains of a woman and child, after a bombing raid on Tokyo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the following two weeks, there were almost 1,600 further <a href="/wiki/Sortie" title="Sortie">sorties</a> against the four cities, destroying 31 square miles (80&#160;km²) in total at a cost of 22 aircraft. By June, over forty percent of the urban area of Japan's largest six cities (Tokyo, Nagoya, Kobe, Osaka, <a href="/wiki/Yokohama" title="Yokohama">Yokohama</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kawasaki,_Kanagawa" title="Kawasaki, Kanagawa">Kawasaki</a>) was devastated. LeMay's fleet of nearly 600 bombers destroyed tens of smaller cities and manufacturing centres in the following weeks and months.</p>
<p>Leaflets were dropped over cities before they were bombed, warning the inhabitants and urging them to escape the city. Though many<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (January 2017)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup>, even within the Air Force, viewed this as a form of <a href="/wiki/Psychological_warfare" title="Psychological warfare">psychological warfare</a>, a significant element in the decision to produce and drop them was the desire to assuage American anxieties about the extent of the destruction created by this new war tactic. Warning leaflets were also dropped on cities not in fact targeted, to create uncertainty and absenteeism.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_kushu_1945-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Tokyo_kushu_1945-3.jpg/220px-Tokyo_kushu_1945-3.jpg" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Tokyo_kushu_1945-3.jpg/330px-Tokyo_kushu_1945-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Tokyo_kushu_1945-3.jpg/440px-Tokyo_kushu_1945-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="644" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_kushu_1945-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Charred remains of victims of one of the attacks on Tokyo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A year after the war, the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Bombing_Survey_(Pacific_War)" class="mw-redirect" title="Strategic Bombing Survey (Pacific War)">U.S. Strategic Bombing Survey</a> reported that American military officials had underestimated the power of strategic bombing combined with naval blockade and previous military defeats to bring Japan to unconditional surrender without invasion. By July 1945, only a fraction of the planned strategic bombing force had been deployed yet there were few targets left worth the effort. In hindsight, it would have been more effective to use land-based and carrier-based air power to strike merchant shipping and begin aerial mining at a much earlier date so as to link up with effective <a href="/wiki/Allied_submarines_in_the_Pacific_War" title="Allied submarines in the Pacific War">submarine anti-shipping campaign</a> and completely isolate the island nation. This would have accelerated the strangulation of Japan and ended the war sooner.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> A postwar <a href="/wiki/Naval_Ordnance_Laboratory" title="Naval Ordnance Laboratory">Naval Ordnance Laboratory</a> survey agreed, finding naval mines dropped by B-29s had accounted for 60% of all Japanese shipping losses in the last six months of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-214">[214]</a></sup> In October 1945, Prince <a href="/wiki/Fumimaro_Konoe" title="Fumimaro Konoe">Fumimaro Konoe</a> said the sinking of Japanese vessels by U.S. aircraft combined with the B-29 aerial mining campaign were just as effective as B-29 attacks on industry alone,<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> though he admitted, "the thing that brought about the determination to make peace was the prolonged bombing by the B-29s." Prime Minister Baron <a href="/wiki/Kantar%C5%8D_Suzuki" title="Kantarō Suzuki">Kantarō Suzuki</a> reported to U.S. military authorities it "seemed to me unavoidable that in the long run Japan would be almost destroyed by air attack so that merely on the basis of the B-29s alone I was convinced that Japan should sue for peace."<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_bombing">Nuclear bombing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Nuclear bombing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nagasaki_temple_destroyed.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Nagasaki_temple_destroyed.jpg/200px-Nagasaki_temple_destroyed.jpg" width="200" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Nagasaki_temple_destroyed.jpg/300px-Nagasaki_temple_destroyed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Nagasaki_temple_destroyed.jpg/400px-Nagasaki_temple_destroyed.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2778" data-file-height="2278" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nagasaki_temple_destroyed.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Nagasaki Prefecture Report on the bombing characterized Nagasaki as "like a graveyard with not a tombstone standing".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While the bombing campaign against Japan continued, the U.S. and its allies were preparing to <a href="/wiki/Operation_Downfall" title="Operation Downfall">invade the Japanese home islands</a>, which they anticipated to be heavily costly in terms of life and property. On 1 April 1945, U.S. troops <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Okinawa" title="Battle of Okinawa">invaded the island of Okinawa</a> and fought there fiercely against not only enemy soldiers, but also enemy civilians. After two and a half months, 12,000 U.S. servicemen, 107,000 Japanese soldiers, and over 150,000 Okinawan civilians (included those forced to fight) were killed. Given the casualty rate in Okinawa, American commanders realized a grisly picture of the intended invasion of mainland Japan. When President <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman" title="Harry S. Truman">Harry S. Truman</a> was briefed on what would happen during an invasion of Japan, he could not afford such a horrendous casualty rate, added to over 400,000 U.S. servicemen who had already died fighting in both the European and Pacific theaters of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nagasakibomb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/170px-Nagasakibomb.jpg" width="170" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/255px-Nagasakibomb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/340px-Nagasakibomb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3245" data-file-height="3877" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nagasakibomb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Mushroom_cloud" title="Mushroom cloud">mushroom cloud</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" title="Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">atomic bombing of Nagasaki, Japan</a>, 1945, rose some 18 km (11 mi) above the <a href="/wiki/Hypocentre" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypocentre">hypocentre</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hoping to forestall the invasion, the United States, the United Kingdom, and the Republic of China issued a <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Declaration" title="Potsdam Declaration">Potsdam Declaration</a> on 26 July 1945, demanding that the Japanese government accept an <a href="/wiki/Unconditional_surrender" title="Unconditional surrender">unconditional surrender</a>. The declaration also stated that if Japan did not surrender, it would be faced with "prompt and utter destruction", a process which was already underway with the incendiary bombing raids destroying 40% of targeted cities, and by naval warfare isolating and starving Japan of imported food. The Japanese government ignored (<i><a href="/wiki/Mokusatsu" title="Mokusatsu">mokusatsu</a></i>) this ultimatum, thus signalling that they were not going to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the wake of this rejection, Stimson and George Marshall (the Army chief of staff) and Hap Arnold (head of the Army Air Forces) set the atomic bombing in motion.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 August 1945, the B-29 bomber <a href="/wiki/Enola_Gay" title="Enola Gay">Enola Gay</a> flew over the Japanese city of Hiroshima in southwest Honshū and dropped a <a href="/wiki/Gun-type_fission_weapon" title="Gun-type fission weapon">gun-type</a> <a href="/wiki/Uranium-235" title="Uranium-235">uranium-235</a> atomic bomb (code-named <a href="/wiki/Little_Boy" title="Little Boy">Little Boy</a> by the U.S.) on it. Two other B-29 aircraft were airborne nearby for the purposes of instrumentation and photography. When the planes first approached Hiroshima, Japanese anti-aircraft units in the city initially thought they were <a href="/wiki/Reconnaissance_aircraft" title="Reconnaissance aircraft">reconnaissance aircraft</a>, since they were ordered not to shoot at one or few aircraft that did not pose a threat, in order to conserve their ammunition for large-scale air raids. The bomb killed roughly 90,000–166,000 people; half of these died quickly while the other half suffered lingering deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-rerf-deaths_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rerf-deaths-219">[219]</a></sup> The death toll included an estimated 20,000 Korean slave laborers and 20,000 Japanese soldiers) and destroyed 48,000 buildings (including the <a href="/wiki/Headquarters" title="Headquarters">headquarters</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Second_General_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Second General Army">Second General Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/5th_Division_(Imperial_Japanese_Army)" title="5th Division (Imperial Japanese Army)">Fifth Division</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-HYO_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HYO-220">[220]</a></sup> On 9 August, three days later, the B-29 <a href="/wiki/Bockscar" title="Bockscar">Bockscar</a> flew over the Japanese city of Nagasaki in northwest Kyushu and dropped an <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon_design#Implosion-type_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon design">implosion-type</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plutonium-239" title="Plutonium-239">plutonium-239</a> atomic bomb (code-named <a href="/wiki/Fat_Man" title="Fat Man">Fat Man</a> by the U.S.) on it, again accompanied by two other B-29 aircraft for instrumentation and photography. This bomb effects killed roughly 39,000–80,000 people,<sup id="cite_ref-rerf-deaths_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rerf-deaths-219">[219]</a></sup> including roughly 23,000–28,000 Japanese war industry employees, an estimated 2,000 Korean forced workers, and at least 150 Japanese soldiers. The bomb destroyed 60% of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-HYO_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HYO-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> The industrial damage in Nagasaki was high, partly owing to the inadvertent targeting of the industrial zone, leaving 68–80% of the non-dock industrial production destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup></p>
<p>Six days after the detonation over Nagasaki, <a href="/wiki/Gyokuon-hoso" class="mw-redirect" title="Gyokuon-hoso">Japan announced</a> <a href="/wiki/Surrender_of_Japan" title="Surrender of Japan">its surrender</a> to the Allied Powers on 15 August 1945, signing the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Instrument_of_Surrender" title="Japanese Instrument of Surrender">Instrument of Surrender</a> on 2 September 1945, officially ending the Pacific War and World War II. The two atomic bombings generated strong sentiments in Japan against all nuclear weapons. Japan adopted the <a href="/wiki/Three_Non-Nuclear_Principles" title="Three Non-Nuclear Principles">Three Non-Nuclear Principles</a>, which forbade the nation from developing nuclear armaments. Across the world anti-nuclear activists have made Hiroshima the central symbol of what they are opposing.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup></p>
